*	(both	energy	related	and	non-energy	related)																
*	Note	that	the	inversion	scheme	uses	the	uncertainty	estimates	only	for	CH4	and	N2O	emissions.							
*	The	current	inversion	scheme	does	not	take	account	of	the	uncertainties	in	the	emissions	of	NOx,	CO,	VOC,	and	SO2.		
*	Two-sigma	prior	error	ranges	in	1950,	1970,	1990,	and	2000	are	300%,	200%,	100%,	100%	of	the	prior	means.			
*	These	factors	are	interpolated	for	the	other	years.														
*	The	factor	of	300%	is	assumed	between	1890	and	1950												
*	For	CH4	and	N2O	before	1890,	the	two-sigma	prior	error	range	is	assumed	to	be	invariant	in	the	absolute	magnitude		
*	(same	as	that	in	1890).																	
*	For	other	gases	before	1890,	the	factor	of	300%	is	also	used.										
*	The	uncertainty	ranges	above	include	some	modifications	of	those	suggested	by	van	Aardenne	(personal	communication).

CONCO2PRI(T)	Data	for	atmospheric	CO2	concentrations	[ppm]																
*	Based	on	the	assumption	that	the	system	in	1750	has	not	been	interfered	from	anthropogenic	activities,						
*	the	CO2	concentration	in	1750	is	fixed	at	the	observational	record	(=	277	ppm)	in	ACC2_init_past.inc.						
*	This	gives	the	estimate	of	the	atmospheric	CO2	load	in	1750	(Variable:	COC1ATMBAC)	by	a	simple	unit	conversion.				
*	Then,	the	model	calculates	the	amount	of	CO2	in	the	ocean	mixed	layer	in	1750							
*	by	reflecting	the	thermodynamic	equilibrium	of	marine	carbonate	chemistry.													
*	Data	sources:																				
*	Etheridge	et	al.	(1996),	1750-1831,	ice	core	data,	75-cutoff	spline,	5-year	intervals,	one-sigma	std	error	of	0,6	ppm				
*	Etheridge	et	al.	(1996),	1832-1968,	ice	core	data,	25-cutoff	spline,	annual,	one-sigma	std	error	of	0,6	ppm					
*	Keeling	et	al.	(2005),	1969-2000,	in	situ	measurements,	annual,	one-sigma	std	error	of	0,1	ppm

RADSOLCRW(T)	Solar	forcing	of	Crowley	-2003	cited	in	Jones	and	Mann	-2004	[W	per	m^2]								
*	Not	used	in	the	standard	ACC2	inversion															
*	The	original	data	that	can	be	obtained	from	http://www.cru.uea.ac.uk/cru/data/paleo/jonesmann04/													
*	are	not	adjusted	to	produce	Figure	7	in	Jones	and	Mann	(2004).										
*	The	original	data	is	the	anomalies	of	solar	radiation	(Lean	et	al.,	1995;	Lean,	2000)	from	the	mean				
*	between	1611	and	1998	(1365.6W/m2).																	
*	The	data	of	Lean	can	be	obtained	from	ftp:													
*	//ftp.ncdc.noaa.gov/pub/data/paleo/climate_forcing/solar_variability/lean2000_irradiance.txt																					
*	The	original	data	needs	to	be	multiplied	by	0,25	and	then	by	0,7	to	be	used	as	radiative	forcing,			
*	according	to	Jones	and	Mann	-2004	p.25	and	26).													
*	The	first	adjustment	is	due	to	the	fact	that	only	the	quarter	of	the	Earth	surface	is	exposed	to	the	Sun	
*	by	assuming	a	perfect	sphere.																	
*	The	second	adjustment	is	due	to	planetary	albedo.	That	is,	30%	of	the	incoming	solar	radiation						
*	reflected	back	to	the	space	at	the	top	of	the	atmosphere.
